 smile by some powdered and embroider french wit to Mme . d'Albany in 
 Alfieri 's hearing ; nay , to Alfieri himself . 

 mix with such meaner , though unconscious motif for dissatisfaction , 
 must have be the sense , intolerable to a man like Alfieri , of the 
 horrid and grotesque jumble of good and bad , of real and false , not 
 merely in the revolutionary movement itself , but in all these man of the 
  ancien régime who initiate it . Alfieri conceive liberty from the 
 purely antique , or , if you prefer , pseudo - antique , point of view ; it 
 be to he the final cause of the world ; the aim of all struggle ; to 
 be free be the one and only desideratum , to be master of one 's own 
 thought , action , and word , merely for the sake of such mastery . the 
 practical advantage of liberty entirely escape he , as do the 
 practical disadvantage of tyranny ; nay , one can almost imagine that 
 have liberty involve absolute misery for all man , and tyranny absolute 
 happiness , Alfieri would have choose liberty . to this pseudo - roman 
 and intensely patrician stoic , who have never know privation or 
 injustice towards himself , and scarcely notice it towards other , 
 the humanitarian , the philanthropic movement , characteristic of the 
 eighteenth century , and which be the strong impulse of the revolution , 
 be absolutely incomprehensible . Alfieri be , in the sense of certain 
 ancient , a hard - hearted man , indifferent , blind and deaf to suffering . 
 that a man of education and mind , a gentleman , should have to sweep the 
 ground with his hat on the passage of another man , because that other 
 happen to wear a ribbon and a star ; that he should be liable to exile , 
 to imprisonment , for a truthful statement of his opinion : these be to 
 Alfieri the insupportable thing of tyranny . but that a man in wooden 
 shoe and a torn smock frock , sleep between the pig and the cow on 
 the damp clay floor , eat bread mainly compose of straw , should have 
 all the profit of his hard labour take from he in taxis , while 
 another man , a splendid gentleman cover over with gold , rid over 
 acre of his land with his hound , or a fat priest dress in silk , 
 snooze over his Lucullus dinner , should be exempt from taxation and 
 empower to starve , rob , beat , or hang the peasant : such a thing as 
 this do not fall within the range of Alfieri 's feeling . to his mind , 
 for ever wrap in an intellectual toga , there be no tragedy in mere 
 misery ; there be no injustice in mere cruelty , or rather misery , 
 cruelty , nay , all their ally evil , ignorance , brutality , sickness , 
 superstition , vice , be unknown to he . hence , as I have say , all the 
 philanthropic side of the revolutionary movement be lose to he ; just 
 as the defence of Labarre , the vindication of Calas , never disturb 
 the current of his contempt for Voltaire . so also the abolition of 
 privilege , the secularisation of church property , the equalisation of 
 legal punishment , the abrogation of barbarous law , the liberation of 
 slave ; all these thing , which stir even the most corrupt and 
 apathetic mind of the late eighteenth century , seem merely so much 
 declamation to Alfieri . to he , who could conceive no virtue beyond 
 independent truthfulness , such thing be mere sentimental trash , mere 
 hypocritical nonsense beneath which base man hide their baseness . and 
 the baseness , unhappily , be there : baseness of absolute corruption , 
 or of scandalous levity , even in the noblest . to Alfieri , a man like 
 Beaumarchais , for all his quick philanthropy , his audacious outspokenness , 
 must have seem base , with his background of money - jobbing , of dirty 
 diplomatic work , of legal squabble . how much more such a man as 
 Mirabeau , with his heroic resolution , his heroic kindliness , his whole 
 Titan nature , carous , eat into by a hundred mean vice . that Mirabeau 
 should have gain his bread write libel and obscene novel , mean to 
 Alfieri not that a man bear in corruption and taint thereby have , by

 movement , raise himself as morally high as he have hitherto grovel

 degrade by a foul writer . 

 from such figure as these Alfieri turn away in indignant disgust . the 
 great movement of the eighteenth century seem to he a mere stirring 
 and splash in a noisome pool , in that cloaca maxima , as he have

 already before settle in Paris in 1787 , he have write to his sienese

 de Staël , André Chénier , Condorcet , Mirabeau , Alfieri could write , with 
 a sort of bitter pleasure at his own narrow - mindedness : " now I be among 
 a million of man , and not one of they that be worth Gori 's little 
 finger . " 

 I be almost prepared to say that Alfieri really feel as if live in 
 Paris , among such people and at such a moment , be a sort of saintly 
 sacrifice , the crown heroism of his life , which he make in order to

 world would be defraud of the great and sovereign antidote to all such 
 baseness as this in the shape of his own complete work . 

 write to his mother towards the end of the year 1788 , he mention 
 contemptuously the excitement and enthusiasm create by the approach 
 election of the States - General , and add calmly : " but all these sort of 
 thing interest I very little ; and I give my attention only to the 
 correction of my proof , a piece of work with which I be pretty well 
 half through . " 




 CHAPTER XV . 

 ENGLAND . 


 the contradiction in complex and self - contradictory character like

 the same note as that even of such a man as Taine . the almost morbid

 CHAPTER XVI . 

 the MISOGALLO . 


 Alfieri and Madame d'Albany be scarcely back in Paris , and settle in 
 a new house , when the disorder in Paris and the movement of the 
 imperial troop on the frontier begin to make the situation of 
 foreigner difficult and dangerous . the storming of the Tuileries , the

 everything to their safety . with considerable difficulty a passport for

 Alfieri from the Venetian Resident   almost the only diplomatic 
 representative , say Alfieri , who still remain to that ghost of a 
 king , and a passport for each of they and for each of their servant

 but Alfieri 's black presentiment hasten it to the 18th . arrive at 
 the Barrière Blanche , on the road to Calais , passport be examine by 
 two or three soldier of the National Guard , and the gate be on the

 suddenly , from out of a neighbouring pot - house , rush some twenty - five 
 or thirty ruffian , ragged , drunken , and furious . they surround the

 to starve without work ; and a crowd rapidly form round they and the 
 National Guards , who want the traveller to be permit to pass on . 
 Alfieri jump out of the carriage , brandish his seven passport , and 
 throw himself , a long , lean , red - haired man , fiercely gesticulate and 
 yelling at the top of his voice , among the crowd , force this man and 
 that to read the passport , cry frantically , " look ! listen ! Name 
 Alfieri . italian and not french ! tall , thin , pale , red - haired ; that be 
 I ; look at I . I have my passport ! we have our passport all in order 
 from the proper authority ! we want to pass ; and , by God ! we will 
 pass ! " 

 after half an hour of this altercation , with voice issue from the 
 crowd , " burn the carriage ! " " throw stone at they ! " " they be run 
 away , they be noble and rich ; take they to the Hotel de Ville to be

 at a country house near Mons , belong to the Countess of Albany 's

 by November Alfieri and Mme . d'Albany be in Florence , safe ; but 
 establish in a miserable inn , without their furniture , their horse ,

 for a moment , with the full luminousness of the tuscan sky once more 
 in his eye , and the guttural strength of the tuscan language once more

 Alfieri have , I feel persuade , become virtually an old man ; his strength

 disappointment , the terror , the horror of the French Revolution become , 
 so to speak , part of a moral illness which last to his death . Alfieri 
 be not a tender - hearted nor a humane man ; have he be , he would have 
 feel more sympathy than he do with the beginning of the great movement , 
 with the striving after reform which precede it ; he have , on the 
 contrary , the sort of cold continuous rage , the ruthless self - righteousness 
 and cut - and - dryness which would have make he , have he be a Frenchman , 
 a terrorist of the most dreadful type ; a regular routinist in extermination 
 of corrupt people . hence I can not believe that , much as he may have be 
 shock by the news of the September massacre , of the grandes 
 fournées which precede Thermidor , and much as he may have be 
 distress by Mme . d'Albany 's anxiety and grief for so many friend who

 that liberty , which he alone be to teach man to desire , should be the 
 fashionable craze , mix up with science , philanthropy , sentiment , and

 the Reign of Terror come to an end , the reaction of Thermidor set

 it be as an expression , an eternal , immortal expression , the severest

 latin and greek author whom Alfieri be busy spell out , do

 Italy , the Misogallo make we like Alfieri even less . whether this 
 revolution , despite the ocean of blood which it shed , might not be

 french invasion , despite the money which it extort , the statue and

 such Alfieri appear to I , and such I think he must appear to everyone

 this French Revolution be merely a revolt of slave ; and what tyranny

 only for slavery ? what be the French ? " the French , " answer one of the 
 epigram of the Misogallo , " have always be puppet ; formerly puppet

 all this political atrabiliousness do not improve Alfieri 's temper ;

 but there be thing to confirm Mme . d'Albany in that easy - go

 a ridiculous man ! not so . I have speak many hard word against Alfieri ; 
 and I repeat that he seem to I to have often fall short , betray by 
 his century , his vanity , his narrowness and hardness of temper , even of 
 the ideal which he have set up for himself . but I would not have it

 of the reality out of which it arise . that Alfieri , a strange mixture of

 idealise poseur , should have fall short of his own ideal , be

 base , whether he be Achilles or Thersites . 

 " uom , sei tu grande o vile ? Mori , il saprai . "   " Man , art thou noble 
 or base ? die , and thou shalt know it . "   thus write Alfieri , make , as 
 usual , fame the arbiter of his worth ; and show , even in the moment of

 fibre , the insufficiency of moral vitality in so many thing ; of

 the letter be to Mme . Teresa Mocenni at Siena , and relate to the death

 of they reduce to a handful of ash . if such a belief as the first be 
 repugnant to physics and to mathematical evidence , it be not , therefore , 
 to be despise . the principal advantage and honour of mankind be that it 
 can feel , and science teach we how not to feel . long live , therefore , 
 ignorance and poetry , and let we accept the imaginary as the true . man 
 subsist upon love ; love make he a god : for I call God an intensely 
 feel love , and I call dog , or French , which come to the same , the 
 frozen philosophiser who be move only by the fact that two and two 
 make four . " 

 Alfieri 's secret desire that he might not survive his beloved be 
 fulfil soon , perhaps , than he expect . the eccentric figure , the

 fly scarlet cloak , drive the well - know phaeton , or saunter 
 moodily along the Lung Arno and through the Boboli gardens , be soon to 
 be see no more . as the year 1803 wear on he feel himself hard press 
 by the gout ; he eat less and less , he take an enormous amount of 
 foot exercise ; he work madly at his memoir , his comedy , his 
 translation , he feel almost constantly fatigued and depressed . on the 
 3rd October 1803 , after his usual morning 's work , he go out for a

 still summer weather , force he to alight and to try and warm himself

 unable to eat or work , and fall into a long drowse ; the next day after

 he refuse to go to bed except at night , and tear off the mustard

 bed , and , without agony or effort , unconscious " like a bird , " say the 
 Countess , give up the ghost . it be between nine and ten of the morning 
 of the 9th October 1803 . Vittorio Alfieri be in his fifty - fifth year . 

 the Abate di Caluso , the great friend he have , after Gori , be 
 summon from Turin to console the Countess and put all paper in order . 
 Alfieri 's will , make out in 1799 , leave all his book and MSS . , and

 among these paper be find a short letter , undated , address " to the 
 friend I have leave behind , Tommaso di Caluso , at Turin , " and which run

 " as I may any day give way beneath the very serious malady which be 
 consume I , I have think it wise to prepare these few line in order

 " I will not give you more pain , at present , by say any more . I have 
 know in you one of the most rare man in every respect . I die love and

 CHAPTER XVIII . 

 FABRE . 


 " happiness have disappear out of the world for I , " write Mme . d'Albany , 
 in January 1804 , to her old friend Canon Luti , at Siena . " I take 
 interest in nothing ; the world might be completely upset without my 
 notice it . I read a little , and reading be the only thing which give 
 I any courage , a merely artificial courage ; for when I return to my 
 own thought and think of all that I have lose , I burst into tear and 
 call death to my assistance , but death will not come . o God ! what a 
 misfortune to lose a person whom one adore and venerate at the same 
 time . I think that if I still have Thérèse   Mme . Mocenni   it would 
 be some consolation ; but there be no consolation for I . I have the 
 strength to hide my feeling before the world , for no one could conceive 
 my misfortune who have not feel it . a twenty - six year ' friendship with 
 so perfect a being , and then to see he take away from I at the very 
 age when I require he most . " 

 Alfieri a perfect being - a being adore and venerate by Mme . d'Albany ! 
 one can not help , in read these word , smile sadly at the strange 
 magic by which death metamorphose those whom he have take in the eye 
 of the survivor ; at the strange potion by mean of which he make love

 enable we to lie to ourselves instead of lie to other . the Countess

 play but a very small part in her colourless life . so small a part , 
 that one may say , without fear of injustice , that Mme . d'Albany have

 fear , and Mme . d'Albany be so little vigilant , so little trouble by

 epitaph , who have settle all his literary affair , who have write the

 the Countess of Albany be not a selfish woman ; she have , apparently

 routinist self - engrossment ; she have be satisfy , or think herself

 thinness and coldness . Alfieri , heaven know , have be selfish and

 while he seem grow daily more fossilised , while he be at once 
 engross with his own scheme of literary glory , and indifferently 
 amuse himself by infidelity to his lady , he be then , even then , 
 constantly haunt by the thought that , unless he himself be leave 
 behind in the terror of widowhood , the Countess of Albany would have to 
 suffer those pang which he feel that he himself could never endure . 

 Alfieri see the Countess through the medium of his own character , and he 
 prove mistaken . perhaps the most terrible ironical retribution which 
 could have fall upon his strange egomania , would have be , have such a 
 thing be possible , the revelation of how gratuitous have be that 
 terrible vision of Mme . d'Albany 's life after his death ; the revelation 
 of how little difference , after the first great grief , his loss have make 
 in her life ; the revelation that , unnoticed , unconsciously , a successor 
 have be prepare for he . 

 in a very melancholy letter , date May 31 , 1804 , in which Mme . d'Albany 
 expatiate to her friend Canon Luti upon the uselessness of her life , 
 and her desire to end it , I find this unobtrusive little sentence : 
 " fabre desire his compliment to you . he have be a great resource to 
 I in everything . " 

 this sentence , I think , explain what to the enemy of Mme . d'Albany 
 have be a delightful scandal , and to her admirer a melancholy mystery ; 
 explain , reduce to mere very simple , conceivable , neither commendable 
 nor shameful every - day prose , the fact that little by little the place 
 leave vacant by Alfieri be fill by another man . italian writer , 
 inheriting from Giordani , even from Foscolo , a certain animosity against 
 a woman who , as soon as Alfieri be dead , become once more what nature 
 have make she , half French , with a great preference for french and french 
 thing - italian writer , I say , have try to turn the Fabre episode 
 into something extremely disgraceful to Mme . d'Albany . Massimo d'Azeglio , 
 partly out of hatred to the Countess , who be rather severe and 
 acrimonious upon his youthful free - and - easiness , partly out of a desire 
 to amuse his reader , have introduce into his autobiography an anecdote

 make eye , kiss his finger , and generally exchange signal with

 amuse by this piece of gossip believe it implicitly ; it do not appear

 openly profligate as that of a South Sea Island village ; and such a 
 society , which could talk of the thing and in the way which it do ,

 take a liking to a man of thirty - five without that liking require a 
 disgusting explanation . the clean explanation seem so much simple and 
 more consonant . Fabre have become an intimate of the house during

 d'Albany , as a friend of the deceased , the brother of his physician , and

 call upon to help in a hundred and one melancholy arrangement : he 
 receive visitor , answered letter , give order ; he probably lay

 Croce , and so forth ; come in contact with the Countess in those manifold

 nothing difficult to understand or shameful to relate in all this ; and 
 the friend of the Countess , delicate - minded woman like Mme . de Souza , 
 puritanic - minded man like Sismondi , misanthropic or scoffing people like 
 Foscolo or Paul Louis Courier , find nothing at which to take umbrage , 
 nothing to rage or laugh at , in this long intimacy between a woman over 
 fifty and a man many year her junior ; a man who live at the other end

 be attach to a woman well know to Mme . d'Albany ; nor have we , I 
 think , any right to be less charitable than they . 

 Louise d'Albany , careless , like most woman of her day , of social 
 institution , and particularly hostile to marriage , be certainly not an 
 impure woman ; her whole life go to prove this . but Louise d'Albany be 
 an indifferent woman , and the extinction of all youthful passion and 
 enthusiasm , the friction of a cynical world , make she daily more 
 indifferent . she have be faithful to Alfieri , devotedly endure one of 
 the most unendurable of companion , love and admire he while he be 
 still alive . but once the pressure of that strong personality remove ,

 from the soft wax of her character . she continue , nay institute , 
 a sort of cultus of Alfieri ; became , as his beloved , the priestess 
 presiding over what have once be his house , and be now his temple . the 
 house on the Lung Arno remain the Casa Alfieri ; the room which he 
 have inhabit be keep carefully untouched ; his book and paper be 
 elaborate and preserve as he have leave they ; his portrait be 
 everywhere , and visitor , like Foscolo , Courier , Sismondi , and the young 
 Lamartine , be expect to inquire respectfully into the legend of the 
 divinity , to ask to see his relic , as the visitor of a shrine might be 
 expect to enquire into the legend , to ask to see the relic , of some 
 great saint . Mme . d'Albany conscientiously devote a portion of her time 
 to see that Alfieri 's work be properly publish , and that 
 Alfieri 's tomb in Santa Croce be properly execute . she be , as I have 
 say , the priestess , the divinely select priestess , of the divinity . but 
 at the same time Mme . d'Albany gradually settle down quite comfortably 
 and happily without Alfieri . after the first great grief be over a 
 sense of relief may have arise , a sense that after all " ' tis an ill 
 wind that blow no good " ; that if she have lose Alfieri she have gain a 
 degree of liberty , of independence , that she have acquire a possibility 
 of be herself with all her taste , the very existence of which she 
 have forget while live under the shadow of that strange and 
 disagreeable great man . a negative sense of compensation , of pleasure 
 in the foreign society to which she could now devote herself ; of 
 satisfaction in the miniature copy of her former parisian salon which 
 she could arrange in her Florentine house ; of comfort in a gently 
 bustling , unconcerned , cheerful old age ; negative feeling which , 
 perhaps as a result of their very repression , seem little by little to 
 have turn to a positive feeling , a positive aversion for the past 
 which she refuse to regret , a positive dislike to the memory of the 
 man whom she could no long love . horrible thing to say ; yet , I 
 fear , true . a man such as Alfieri have permit himself to become , 
 admirable in many respect , but intolerant , hard , arrogant , selfish , 
 self - engross , can not really be love ; he may be endure as a result of 
 long habit , he may inflict his personality without effort upon another ; 
 but in order that this be the case that other must be singularly 
 apathetic , indifferent , malleable ; and apathetic , indifferent , and 
 malleable people , those who never resist the live individual , rarely 
 remember the dead one . " she be , " write one of the most conscientious 
 and respectful of man , the late Gino Capponi , " heavy in feature and 
 form , and , if I may say so , her mind , like her body , be thick - set .... 
 since several year she have cease to love Alfieri . " 

 we can not be indignant with she ; she have never pretend to be what she 
 be not . a highly intellectual , literary mind , a pure temperament , a 
 passive , rather characterless character , take the impress of its 
 surrounding ; passionate when Alfieri be passionate , depressed when 
 Alfieri be depressed ; cheerful when Alfieri 's successor , Fabre and 
 mankind and womankind in general , be cheerful . to be angry with such a 
 woman would be ridiculous ; but , little as we may feel attach to the 
 memory of Alfieri , we can not help say to ourselves , " thank Heaven he 
 never understand what she be ; thank Heaven he never foresaw what she 
 would be ! " 




 CHAPTER XIX . 

 SALON of the COUNTESS . 


 a shadowy being , nay , a shadow cast in the unmistakable shape of 
 another , so long as Alfieri be alive , the Countess of Albany seem to 
 gain consistency and form , to become a substantive person , only after 
 Alfieri 's death . this woman , whom , in the last ten year , we have see 
 consort almost exclusively with Italians , and spend the great 
 proportion of her day in solitary reading of Condillac , Lock , Kant , 
 Mme . de Genlis , Lessing , Milton , everything and anything ; whose letter , 
 exclusively   as far as I know they   to Italians of the middle class , 
 be full of fury against everything that be french ; this woman , who have 
 hitherto be a feeble replica of Alfieri , suddenly turn into an 
 extremely sociable , chatty woman of the world , and a woman of the world 
 who be , to all intent and purpose , French . 

 to be the rallying point of a very cosmopolitan , literary , but by no 
 mean unworldly society , seem suddenly to have become Mme . d'Albany 's 
 mission ; and read the letter copy from the Montpellier Archives , 
 and publish by M. Saint René Taillandier , one wonder how this friend 
 of Mme . de Staël , of Sismondi , of Mme . de Souza , this hostess of Moore , 
 of Lamartine , of Lady Morgan , of every sort of french , English , german , 
 Russian , or polyglot creature of distinction that travel through 
 Italy in the early part of this century , could ever have be the 
 beloved of Alfieri , the misanthropic correspondent of a lot of sienese 
 professor , priest , and shop - keeper . 

 the fact be that Mme . d'Albany could now become , so to speak , what she 
 really be ; or , at least , show herself to be such . worldly wise and a 
 trifle cynical she have always be ; in the midst of the page of literary 
 review and political newspaper constitute her letter to Mme . Mocenni , 
 Canon Luti and Alessandro Cerretani of Siena , there be a good deal of 
 mere personal gossip , story of married woman 's lover , married man 's 
 mistress , domestic bickering ,   c. , intersperse with very plain - speak 
 and   accord to our idea   slightly demoralise moralising . it be 
 evident that this be not a woman to shrink from the reality of thing , 
 to take the world in disgust , to expect too much of her acquaintance . 
 on the other hand these letter of the Alfieri period show Mme . d'Albany 
 to have be decidedly a good - natured and friendly woman . she have the 
 gift of get people to trust she with their little annoyance and 
 grievance ; she be constantly administer sympathy to Mme . Mocenni 
 for the tiresomeness and stupidity and harshness of her husband ; she 
 keep up a long correspondence , recommend book , correct french 
 exercise , exhort to study and to virtue   particularly to abstinence 
 from gambling , encouraging , help Mme . Mocenni 's boy Vittorio . she be 
 clearly a woman who enjoy hear about other folk 's concern , enjoy 
 take an interest in they , sympathise and , if possible , assist 
 they . 

 these two quality , a dose of cynical worldliness , sufficient to 
 prevent all squeamishness and that coldness and harshness which spring 
 from expect people to be well than they be , and a dose of 
 kindliness , helpfulness , pleasure in know the affair and feeling 
 and trouble of other ; these two quality be , I should think , the 
 essential for a woman who would keep a salon in the old sense of the 
 word , who would be the centre of a large but decidedly select society , 
 the friend and correspondent of many and various people possess of 
 more genius or more character than herself . such a woman , thank to she 
 easy - go knowledge of the world , and to her cordial curiosity and 
 helpfulness , be the friend of the most hostile people ; and she be so 
 completely satisfied with , and interested in , the particular person with 
 whom she be talk or to whom she be write , that that particular 
 person really believe himself or herself to be her chief friend , and 
 overlook the score of other chief friend , view with exactly the 
 same degree of interest , and treat with the same degree of cordiality 
 all round . the world be apt to like such woman , as such woman like it , 
 and to say of they that there must be an immense richness of character , 
 an extraordinary power of bring out the good quality of every 
 individual , in a woman who can drive such complicated team of friend . 
 but be it not more probable that the secret of such success be poverty 
 of personality rather than richness ; and that so many people receive a 
 share of friendship , of sympathy , of comprehension , because each 
 receive only very little ; because the universal friend be too obtuse to 
 mind anybody 's fault , and too obtuse , also , to mind anybody 's great 
 virtue ? in short , do not such woman pay people merely in the paper 
 money of attention , which can be multiply at pleasure , rather than in 
 the gold coin of sympathy , of which the supply be extremely small ? 

 be this as it may , Mme . d'Albany , after have be , in the early 
 period of her life , essentially the woman who have one friend , who let 
 the wax of her nature be stamp in one clear die , became , in the twenty 
 year which separate the death of Alfieri from her own , pre - eminently 
 the woman with many friend , a blurred personality in which we recognise 
 trace of the mental effigy of many and various people . Mme . d'Albany 
 be , therefore , in superficial sympathy with nearly everyone , and in 
 deep antagonism with no one : she be the ideal of the woman who keep a 
 literary and political salon . at that time especially , when Italy be 
 visit only by people of a certain social standing , society be carry 
 on by a most complicated system of letter of introduction , and everyone 
 of any note bring a letter to Mme . d'Albany . " La grande lanterne 
 magique passe tout par votre salon , " write Sismondi to the Countess ; 
 and the metaphor could not be truer . writer and artist , beautiful 
 woman , diplomatist , journalist , pedant , man of science , woman of 
 fashion , Châteaubriand and Mme . de Staël , Lamartine and Paul Louis 
 Courier , Mme . Récamier and the Duchess of Devonshire , Canova and 
 Foscolo , and Sismondi and Werner , the whole intellectual world of the 
 Empire and the Restoration , all seem to be project , figure now 
 flit past like shadow , now dwell long , clear and colour , upon 
 the rather colourless and patternless background of Mme . d'Albany 's 
 house ; nay , of Mme . d'Albany herself . such reader as may wish to have 
 all these figure , remember or forget , point out to they , call 
 by their right name and title , treat with the perfect impartiality 
 of a valet de place expound monument , or of a chamberlain

 Baron Alfred von Reumont ; and such reader   and I hope they be more 
 numerous   as may wish to examine some of the nobler and more interesting

 Staël to the Countess of Albany , and the interesting page of criticism 
 in which they have be imbed by M. St.-René Taillandier . with regard 
 to myself , I feel that the time and space which have be give I in 
 order to analyse or reconstruct the curious type and curious individual 
 call Louise d'Albany be both nearly exhausted ; and I can therefore 
 select to dwell upon , of these many magic - lantern man and woman , of 
 these friend of the Countess , only two , because they seem to I to 
 exemplify my remark about the friendship of a woman whose vocation it 
 be to have many friend . the two be Sismondi and Foscolo . 

 two or three year after Alfieri 's death , somewhere about the year 1806 
 or 1807 , there be introduce to Mme . d'Albany a sort of half - italian , 
 half - french Swiss , a man young in year and singularly young - with the 
 peculiar earnestness , gravity , purity which belong sometimes to 
 youth - in spirit , Jean Charles Léonard Simonde de Sismondi . quietly 
 idealistic , with one of those northern , eminently protestant mind which 
 imagine the principle of good to be more solemnly serious , the principle 
 of evil more vainly negative , than be , alas , the case in this world - M. 
 de Sismondi , full of the heroism of mediæval Italy which he be study 
 with a view to his great work , come to the house of Alfieri , to the 
 woman whom Alfieri have love , as to thing most reverend and almost 
 sacred . the Countess of Albany receive he very well ; and this good 
 reception , the motherly cordiality of this woman with that light in her 
 hazel eye , that welcome graciousness in the line of her mouth , which 
 Lamartine have charmingly describe , with the " parole suave , manière 
 san apprêt , familiarité rassurante , " " which make one doubt whether she 
 be descend to the level of her visitor , or raise he up to her 
 own , " - this reception by this woman , who be , moreover , still surround 
 by a halo of Alfieri 's glory , fairly conquer the heart , the pure ,

 his way between Geneva , whither he be call by his family business and 
 his lecture , and Pescia , a little town nestle among the olive of the 
 Lucchese Apennine , where he be for ever sigh to join his mother , to

 house on the Lung Arno , have an almost romantic fascination for Sismondi ; 
 those pass visit , at interval of month , when Mme . d'Albany would

 feel that   listen to the young man 's enthusiastic talk about liberty , 
 letter , and philanthropy , about Alfieri and Mme . de Staël , enable 
 Sismondi to make up for himself a sort of half - imaginary Countess of 
 Albany , to whom he pour out all his hope and fear in innumerable 
 letter , for whom he long as   alas !   we perhaps long only for the 
 phantom of our own creating . that Mme . d'Albany be , after all , a 
 shallow woman ; that she adore a mediocre M. Fabre   to whom Sismondi 
 invariably send respectful message   and half dislike the memory of 
 Alfieri ; that she have call Mme . de Staël , Sismondi 's goddess , about 
 whom he be for ever expatiating , " a mad woman who always want to 
 inspire passion , and feel nothing , and make her reader feel nothing " 
  I be quote from an unpublished letter at Siena ; that she prefer 
 despotism on the whole to liberty , and have no particular belief or 
 interest in the heroic thing of the present and future ; that she be a 
 lover of gossip and scandal , sometimes   as Gino Capponi say   hard and 
 disagreeable ; that she inspire some man , like d'Azeglio and Giordani , 
 with a positive repulsion as a vulgar - minded , spiteful , meddlesome old 
 thing ; that there should be any other Mme . d'Albany than the one of his 
 noble fancy , than the woman whose image   fashion by himself   he love 
 to unite with the image of his own sweet , serious , shy , noble - minded 
 mother : all these thing M. de Sismondi , who never guess himself to be 
 otherwise than the most unpoetical and practical of man , never dream 
 of . so Sismondi go on writing to Mme . d'Albany , pour out his grief 
 at Mme . de Staël 's persecution , his scheme of general improvement , all 
 the interest which fill his gentle , austere , and enthusiastic mind . 
 1814 come , and 1815 . Sismondi have always hat , with the hatred of an 
 italian mediæval patriot , and the hatred of an eighteenth - century 
 philanthropist , the despotism , the bureaucratic levelling , the great 
 military slaughter of Napoleon ; but when he see Napoleon succeed by 
 the inept and wicked government of the Restoration , his heart seem to 
 burst . a Swiss , scarcely acquaint with France , the passion for the 
 principle of liberty and good sense and progress which France have 
 represent , the passion for France itself , burst out in he with 
 generous ardour . this man suffer intensely at what to he , as to Byron 
 and to Shelley   we must recollect the introduction of the Revolt of 
 Islam   , seem the battle between progress and retrogression ; and 
 suffer all the more as he be too pure and just - minded not to feel the 
 impossibility of complete sympathy with either side . Mme . d'Albany 
 answer his letter with olympic serenity . what be it to she which get 
 the upper hand ? she be by this time one of those placid mixture of 
 optimism and pessimism which do not expect good to triumph , simply 
 because they do not care whether good do triumph . Sismondi , in his 
 adoration of she , think this might be the result of a superior 
 magnanimity of character ; yet he keep conjure she to take an interest 
 in the tragedy which be take place before her eye . if she will take 
 no interest , will not fabre ? " do M. Fabre not feel himself turn 
 French again ? " write Sismondi , and there be a pathetic insistency 
 in the question . Fabre think of his picture , his collection of 
 antique , perhaps of his dinner ; of anything save France and political 
 event . Mme . d'Albany smile serenely , and chaff Sismondi a little for 
 his political passion . Sismondi , of all man the most loyal to the idea 
 he have form of his friend , seem never to have permit himself to 
 see the real woman , the real abyss of indifference , beneath his ideal 
 Mme . d'Albany . but there be few thing more pathetic , I think , than the 
 letter of this enthusiastic man to this cold woman ; than the belief of 
 Sismondi - writing that the retrograde measure of which he read in the 
 paper give he fit of fever , that the post day on which he expect 
 political news be day of frenzied expectation - in the moral fibre , 
 the faculty for indignation , of this pleasant , indifferent , cynical 
 quasi - widow of Alfieri . 

 the story of the Countess and Foscolo be an even sad instance of 
 those melancholy little psychological drama which go on , unseen to the 
 world , in a man 's soul ; little drama without outward event , without 
 death or parting or such - like similar visible catastrophe , but the 
 action of which be the slow murder of an affection , of an ideal , of a 
 belief in the loyalty , sympathy , and comprehension of another . the 
 character and history of Ugo Foscolo , like Chénier , half a Greek in 
 blood , and more than half a Greek in passionate love of beauty and 
 indomitable love of liberty , be amongst the most interesting in italian 
 literature ; and I regret that I can say but little of they in this 
 place . review his brief life , his long career from the moment when , 
 scarcely more than a boy , he have enter the service of liberty as a 
 soldier , a political writer , and a poet , only to taste the bitterness of 
 the betrayal of Campo Formio , he write , in 1823 , from London , where he 
 be slowly die , to his sister Rubina : " I be now nearly forty - six ; 
 and you , although young than myself , can recollect how miserable , 
 how unquiet and uncertain our life have always be ever since our 
 childhood . " poor , vain , passionate and proud , tear between the selfish 
 impulse of an exactingly sensuous and imaginative nature , and the rigid 
 sense of duty of a heroic and generous mind , Ugo Foscolo be one of the 
 early and most genuine victim of that sickness of disappointed hope 
 and betray enthusiasm , of that Weltschmerz of which personal 
 misfortune seem as but the least dreadful part , that come upon the 
 noble mind after the Revolution , and which he have paint , with 
 great energy and truthfulness , in his early novel Jacopo Ortis . his 
 career break by his determination never to come to term with any 
 sort of baseness , his happiness destroy by political disappointment , 
 literary feud , and a number of love affair into which his weak , more 
 passionate and vainer , yet not more ungenerous temper be for ever 
 embroil he , Foscolo come to Florence , ill and miserable , in the year 
 1812 . the Countess of Albany , recognise in he a something - a mixture 
 of independence , of passion , of vanity , of truthfulness , of pose - which 
 resemble Alfieri in his early day   though , as she be unable to 
 see , a nobler Alfieri , wider - minded , warmer - hearte , bear in a nobler 
 civilization and destine to give to Italy a nobler example , the pattern 
 for her Leopardi , than Alfieri have be able to give   - the Countess of 
 Albany receive Foscolo well . his letter be full of allusion to the 
 hour which he spend seat at the little round table in Mme . d'Albany 's 
 drawing - room , opposite to the " Muse " newly buy of Canova , narrate 
 to she his many and tangled love affair ; love affair in which he leave 
 his heart on all the briar , and in which , however , by an instinct which 
 show the very nobleness of his nature , he seem to have be impel 
 rather towards woman whom he must love sincerely and unhappily , than 
 towards Marchesa di Prié and Lady Ligonier , like Alfieri ; love affair 
 in which , alas , there be also a good dose of the vanity of a poet and a 
 notorious beau . Mme . d'Albany , as we have see , love gossip ; and , be 
 a kind , helpful woman , she also sincerely like become the confidant 
 of other folk 's woe . she take a real affection for this strange 
 Foscolo . Foscolo , in return , ill , sore of heart , solitary , gradually 
 get to love this gentle , sympathise Countess with a sort of filial 
 devotion , but a filial devotion into which there enter also somewhat 
 of the feeling of a wound man towards his nurse , of the feeling of a 
 devout man towards his Madonna . 

 his letter be full of this feeling : " my friend and not the friend of 
 my good fortune , " he write to Mme . d'Albany in 1813 , " I seem to have 
 leave home , mother , friend , and almost the person dear to my heart in 
 leave Florence . " again , " I have in you , mia Signora , a friend and a 
 mother ; a person , in short , such as no name can express , but such as 
 suffice to console I in the misery which be perhaps incurable 
 and interminable . " her letter be a real ray of sunlight in his 
 gloomy life , they be ' so full of graciousness , and condescension and 
 benevolence and love . I venture to use this last word , because I feel 
 the sentiment which it express in myself towards you . " 

 his health , his work , his money - matter , his love - affair , be all 
 get into a more and more lamentable condition , in which Mme . 
 d'Albany 's sympathy come as a blessing , when the catastrophe of 
 1814 and 1815 , which to Italy mean the commencement of a state of 
 degradation and misery much more intolerable and hopeless than any 
 previous one , come and drown the various bitterness of poor 
 Foscolo 's life in a sea of bitterness . " Italy , " write Foscolo to Mme . 
 d'Albany in 1814 , " be a corpse ; and a corpse which must not be touch 
 if the stench thereof be not to be make more horrible . and yet I see 
 certain crazy creature fantasticate way of bring she to life ; for 
 myself , I should wish she to be bury with myself , and overwhelm by 
 the sea , or that some new Phaeton should precipitate upon her the 
 flaming heaven , so that the ash should be scatter to the four 
 wind , and that the nation come and to come should forget the infamy 
 of our time . amen . " 

 how strongly we feel in this outburst that , despite his despair , or 
 perhaps on account of it , Foscolo be himself one of those " crazy 
 creature fantasticate way of bring Italy to life ! " but the 
 Countess do not understand ; she could conceive like Bonaparte and 
 serve he , or like the restoration and serve it ; but to love an 
 abstract Italy which do not yet exist , to hate equally all those who 
 deprive it of freedom , that be not within her comprehension . and as 
 she could not comprehend this feeling , the mainspring of Foscolo 's soul , 
 so she could understand of Foscolo only the slighter , mean thing : his 
 trouble and intrigue , his love and quarrel . the moment come when the 
 grief of miscomprehension be reveal to poor Foscolo ; when he see 
 how little he be understand by this woman whom he love as a mother . 
 Foscolo have refuse , latterly , to serve Napoleon ; he refuse , also , 
 to serve the Austrians . hat for his independent way both by the 
 Bonapartists and the reactionist , surround by spy , he be force 
 to quit Italy never to return . he write to explain his motif to Mme . 
 d'Albany . Mme . d'Albany write back in a way which show that she 
 believe the assertion of Foscolo 's enemy ; that she ascribe to 
 cowardice , to meanness , to a base desire to make himself conspicuous , 
 the self - inflict exile which he have take upon he : a letter which the 
 editor of Foscolo 's correspondence describe to we in one 
 word - unworthy . 

 this letter come upon Foscolo like a thunder - clap . " so thus , " he write 
 to the Countess in August 1815 , " generosity and justice be banish 
 even from nobler soul . your letter , Signora Contessa , grieve I , and 
 confer upon I , at the same time , two advantage : it diminish 
 suddenly the perpetual nostalgia which I have feel for Florence , and it 
 afford I an occasion to try my strength of spirit .... my hatred for 
 the tyranny with which Bonaparte be oppress Italy do not imply 
 that I should love the house of Austria . the difference for I be 
 that I hop that Bonaparte 's ambition might bring about , if not the 
 independence of Italy , at least such magnanimous deed as might raise 
 the Italians ; whereas the regular government of Austria preclude all 
 such hope . I should be mad and infamous if I desire for Italy , which 
 require peace at any price , new disorder and slaughtering ; but I 
 should consider myself madder still and more infamous if , have despise 
 to serve the foreigner who have fall , I should accept to serve the 
 foreigner who have succeed .... but if your accusation of inconstancy be 
 unjust , your accusation that I want to ' passer pour original ' be 
 actually offensive and mock . " 

 later , in his solitary wandering , Foscolo 's heart seem to have melt 
 towards his former friend ; he write her one or two letter , conciliate , 
 friendly , but how different from the former one ! the Countess of 
 Albany , whom he have love and trust , be dead ; the woman who remain 
 be dear to he as a mere relic of that dead ideal . 

 such be the story of Mme . d'Albany 's friendship for two of the noble 
 spirit , Sismondi and Foscolo , of their day ; the noble , the one in his 
 pure austerity , the other in his magnanimous passionateness , that ever 
 cross the path of the beloved of Alfieri . 




 CHAPTER XX . 

 SANTA CROCE . 


 with her other friend , who give less of their own heart and ask less 
 of her , Mme . d'Albany be more fortunate . she contrive to connect 
 herself by correspondence with the most eminent man and woman of the 
 most different view and temper ; she make her salon in Florence , as M. 
 St. René Taillandier have observe , a sort of adjunct to the cosmopolitan 
 salon of Mme . de Staël at Coppet . her effort in so doing be crown 
 with the very high success . in 1809 Napoleon request Mme . d'Albany 
 to leave Florence for Paris , where , he add with a mixture of brutality 
 and sarcasm , she might indulge her love of art in the new gallery of 
 the Louvre , and where her social talent could no long spread 
 dissatisfaction with his government , as be the case in Italy . 

 the one year 's residence in Paris , which Napoleon 's jealous meddlesomeness 
 force upon she , be , in itself , a very enjoyable time , spend with the 
 friend whom she have leave in ' 93 , and with a whole host of new one whom 
 she have make since . she return to Florence with a large number of 
 devoted correspondent than ever ; her salon become more and more brilliant ; 
 and when , after Waterloo , the whole english world of politic , fashion , 
 and letter pour on to the Continent , her house become , as Sismondi 
 say , the wall on which all the most brilliant figure of the great 
 magic lantern be project . 

 thus , see crowd of the most distinguished and delightful people , 
 receive pile of the most interesting and adore letter , happy , 
 self - satisfy , Mme . d'Albany grow into an old woman . every evening 
 until ten , the room of the Casa Alfieri be throw open ; the servant 
 in the Stuart livery usher in the guest , the tea be serve in 
 those famous service emblazon with the royal arm of England . the 
 Countess have not yet abandon her regal pretension ; for all her 
 condescend cordiality towards the elect , she could assume air of 
 social superiority which some folk scarcely brook , and she be 
 evidently pleased when , half in earnest , Mme . de Staël address she as 
 " my dear Sovereign , " " my dear Queen , " and even when that vulgar woman of 
 genius , Lady Morgan , make a buffoonish scene about the " dead usurper , " 
 on the death of George III . but Mme . d'Albany herself be get to 
 look and talk less and less like a queen , either the Queen of Great 
 Britain or the queen of Hearts ; she be fat , squat , snub , dress with 
 an eternal red shawl   now the property of an intimate friend of mine , 
 in a dress extremely suggestive of an old house - keeper . she be , when 
 not do the queen , cordial , cheerful in manner , love to have 
 child about she , to spoil they with cake and see they romp and 
 dance ; free and easy , cynical , Rabelaisian , if I may use the expression , 
 as such mongrel Frenchwomen be apt to grow with year ; the nick - name 
 which she give to a member of a family where the tradition of she and 
 her way still persist , reveal a wealth of coarse fun which be rather 
 strange in a woman who be once the Beatrice or Laura of a poet . she be 
 active , mentally and bodily , never give up her multifarious reading , 
 her letter - writing ; never forego her invariable morning walk , in a 
 big bonnet and the legendary red shawl , down the Lung Arno and into the 
 Cascine . 

 such be Louise of Stolberg , Countess of Albany , widow of Prince Charles 
 Edward , widow , in a sense , of the poet Vittorio Alfieri ; and such , at 
 the age of seventy - two , do death overtake she , on the 29th January 
 1824 . her property she bequeath to Fabre whom a false rumour have 
 call her husband ; and Fabre leave it jointly to his native town of 
 Montpellier , and to his friend the Cavaliere Emilio Santarelli , who 
 still live and recollect Mme . d'Albany . 

 the famous epitaph , compose by Alfieri for himself , have be mangle by 
 Mme . d'Albany and those who help she and Canova in devise his tomb ; 
 the companion epitaph , the one in which Alfieri describe the Countess 
 as bury next to he , be also mangle in its adaptation to a tomb 
 erect in Santa Croce , entirely separate from Alfieri 's . on that 
 monument of Mme . d'Albany , in the chapel where moulder the fresco of 
 Masolino , there be not a word of that sentence of Alfieri 's about the 
 dead woman have be to he dearer and more respected than any other 
 human thing . Mme . d'Albany have change into quite another be between 
 1803 and 1824 ; the friend of Sismondi , of Foscolo , of Mme . de Staël , the 
 worldly friend of many friend , seem to have no connection with the 
 lady who have weep for Alfieri in the convent at Rome , who have bear 
 with all Alfieri 's misanthropic fury after the Revolution , any more 
 than with the delicate intellectual girl whom Charles Edward have nearly 
 do to death in his drunken jealousy . so , on the whole , Fabre , and 
 whosoever assist Fabre , be right in concoct a new epitaph . 

 but to we , who have follow the career - whose lesson be that of the 
 meanness which lurk in noble thing , the nobility which lurk in mean 
 one - of this woman from her inauspicious wedding - day to the placid day 
 of her death , to we Louise of Stolberg , Countess of Albany , queen of 
 Great Britain , France , and Ireland , will remain , for all blame we 
 may give she and her time , a figure to remember and reflect upon , 
 principally because of those suppress word of her epitaph : " A 
 Victorio Alferio ultra re omne dilecta , et quasi mortale numen ab 
 ipso constanter habita et observata . "
